<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>th root</h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Arithmetic operation</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about nth-roots of real and complex numbers. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Root_(disambiguation)#Mathematics" title="Root (disambiguation)">Root (disambiguation) § Mathematics</a>.</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, an <b><i>n</i>th root</b> of a <a href="/wiki/Number" title="Number">number</a> <i>x</i> is a number <i>r</i> which, when raised to the power <i>n</i>, yields <i>x</i>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r^{n}=x,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>r</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r^{n}=x,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle r^{n}=x,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c22cbcdc8f114887cf0ceeb723bb9624c6f132e2" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:7.342ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>where <i>n</i> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Positive_integer" title="Positive integer">positive integer</a>, sometimes called the <i>degree</i> of the root.  A root of degree 2 is called a <i><a href="/wiki/Square_root" title="Square root">square root</a></i> and a root of degree 3, a <i><a href="/wiki/Cube_root" title="Cube root">cube root</a></i>. Roots of higher degree are referred by using ordinal numbers, as in <i>fourth root</i>, <i>twentieth root</i>, etc.  The computation of an <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>th root is a <b>root extraction</b>.
</p><p>For example, 3 is a square root of 9, since 3<sup>2</sup> = 9, and −3 is also a square root of 9, since (−3)<sup>2</sup> = 9.
</p><p>Any non-zero number considered as a <a href="/wiki/Complex_number" title="Complex number">complex number</a> has <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> different complex <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>th roots, including the <a href="/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">real</a> ones (at most two). The <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>th root of 0 is zero for all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Positive_integer" title="Positive integer">positive integers</a> <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>, since <span class="texhtml">0<sup><i>n</i></sup> = 0</span>. In particular, if <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> is even and <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i></span> is a positive real number, one of its <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>th roots is real and positive, one is negative, and the others (when <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> &gt; 2</span>) are non-real <a href="/wiki/Complex_number" title="Complex number">complex numbers</a>; if <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> is even and <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i></span> is a negative real number, none of the <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>th roots is real. If <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> is odd and <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i></span> is real, one <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>th root is real and has the same sign as <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i></span>, while the other (<span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> – 1</span>) roots are not real. Finally, if <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i></span> is not real, then none of its <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>th roots are real.
</p><p>Roots of real numbers are usually written using the <a href="/wiki/Radical_symbol" title="Radical symbol">radical symbol</a> or <i>radix</i> <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {{~^{~}}^{~}\!\!}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msup>
<mtext> </mtext>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext> </mtext>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext> </mtext>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mspace width="negativethinmathspace"></mspace>
<mspace width="negativethinmathspace"></mspace>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt {{~^{~}}^{~}\!\!}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {{~^{~}}^{~}\!\!}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0a087bedf56ce21d91007bc1ae516b3d792a0b09" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; margin-right: -0.774ex; width:4.142ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>, with <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mi>x</mi>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt {x}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\sqrt {x}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d62b24be305beff66cba9bfbcc01a362ba390f44" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:3.266ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> denoting the positive square root of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> if <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> is positive; for higher roots, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mroot>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</mroot>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\sqrt[{n}]{x}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7b3ba2638d05cd9ed8dafae7e34986399e48ea99" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:3.266ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> denotes the real <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>th root if <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> is odd, and the positive <i>n</i>th root if <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span> is even and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> is positive. In the other cases, the symbol is not commonly used as being ambiguous. In the expression <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mroot>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</mroot>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\sqrt[{n}]{x}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7b3ba2638d05cd9ed8dafae7e34986399e48ea99" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:3.266ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>, the integer <i>n</i> is called the <i>index</i> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> is called the <i>radicand</i>. 
</p><p>When complex <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th roots are considered, it is often useful to choose one of the roots, called <b>principal root</b>, as a <a href="/wiki/Principal_value" title="Principal value">principal value</a>. The common choice is to choose the principal <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th root of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> as the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th root with the greatest real part, and when there are two (for <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> real and negative), the one with a positive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imaginary_part" title="Imaginary part">imaginary part</a>. This makes the <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th root a <a href="/wiki/Function_(mathematics)" title="Function (mathematics)">function</a> that is real and positive for <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> real and positive, and is <a href="/wiki/Continuous_function" title="Continuous function">continuous</a> in the whole <a href="/wiki/Complex_plane" title="Complex plane">complex plane</a>, except for values of <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">x</span> that are real and negative. 
</p><p>A difficulty with this choice is that, for a negative real number and an odd index, the principal <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th root is not the real one. For example, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle -8}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>8</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle -8}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle -8}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b24cf97579cf40493908c64dc45971c781c97e78" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:2.971ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> has three cube roots, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle -2}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</math></span><img alt="1+i{\sqrt  {3}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/11e64063ae461766db09ab330a3dc78add987ae6" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.55ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>
</p><p>An unresolved root, especially one using the radical symbol, is sometimes referred to as a <i><b>surd</b></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> or a <i><b>radical</b></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silver_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-silver-2">[2]</a></sup> Any expression containing a radical, whether it is a square root, a cube root, or a higher root, is called a <i><b>radical expression</b></i>, and if it contains no <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcendental_functions" title="Transcendental functions">transcendental functions</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcendental_numbers" title="Transcendental numbers">transcendental numbers</a> it is called an <i><a href="/wiki/Algebraic_expression" title="Algebraic expression">algebraic expression</a></i>.
</p><p>Roots can also be defined as special cases of <a href="/wiki/Exponentiation" title="Exponentiation">exponentiation</a>, where the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exponent" title="Exponent">exponent</a> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fraction_(mathematics)" title="Fraction (mathematics)">fraction</a>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}=x^{1/n}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</tr></tbody></table></div>
<p>Roots are used for determining the <a href="/wiki/Radius_of_convergence" title="Radius of convergence">radius of convergence</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Power_series" title="Power series">power series</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Root_test" title="Root test">root test</a>. The <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">n</span>th roots of 1 are called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roots_of_unity" title="Roots of unity">roots of unity</a> and play a fundamental role in various areas of mathematics, such as <a href="/wiki/Number_theory" title="Number theory">number theory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_equations" title="Theory of equations">theory of equations</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fourier_transform" title="Fourier transform">Fourier transform</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Square_root#History" title="Square root">Square root § History</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cube_root#History" title="Cube root">Cube root § History</a></div>
<p>An archaic term for the operation of taking <i>n</i>th roots is <i>radication</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Definition_and_notation">Definition and notation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Definition and notation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NegativeOne4Root.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="480" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/NegativeOne4Root.svg/220px-NegativeOne4Root.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/NegativeOne4Root.svg/330px-NegativeOne4Root.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/NegativeOne4Root.svg/440px-NegativeOne4Root.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NegativeOne4Root.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The four 4th roots of −1,<br/> none of which are real</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NegativeOne3Root.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="480" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/NegativeOne3Root.svg/220px-NegativeOne3Root.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/NegativeOne3Root.svg/330px-NegativeOne3Root.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/NegativeOne3Root.svg/440px-NegativeOne3Root.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NegativeOne3Root.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The three 3rd roots of −1,<br/> one of which is a negative real</div></div></div>
<p>An  <b><i>n</i>th root</b> of a number <i>x</i>, where <i>n</i> is a positive integer, is any of the <i>n</i> real or complex numbers <i>r</i> whose <i>n</i>th power is <i>x</i>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r^{n}=x.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>r</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r^{n}=x.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle r^{n}=x.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e193fe7a53ebc7310d4ca7c0b9bbdb6b262af50f" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.342ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Every positive <a href="/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">real number</a> <i>x</i> has a single positive <i>n</i>th root, called the <a href="/wiki/Principal_value" title="Principal value">principal <i>n</i>th root</a>, which is written <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mroot>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</mroot>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\sqrt[{n}]{x}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7b3ba2638d05cd9ed8dafae7e34986399e48ea99" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:3.266ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>. For <i>n</i> equal to 2 this is called the principal square root and the  <i>n</i> is omitted. The <i>n</i>th root can also be represented using <a href="/wiki/Exponentiation" title="Exponentiation">exponentiation</a> as <i>x</i><sup>1/n</sup>.
</p><p>For even values of <i>n</i>, positive numbers also have a negative <i>n</i>th root, while negative numbers do not have a real <i>n</i>th root.  For odd values of <i>n</i>, every negative number <i>x</i> has a real negative <i>n</i>th root.  For example, −2 has a real 5th root, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{5}]{-2}}=-1.148698354\ldots }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mroot>
<mrow>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>5</mn>
</mrow>
</mroot>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1.148698354</mn>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{5}]{-2}}=-1.148698354\ldots }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{5}]{-2}}=-1.148698354\ldots }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/98d22c0a8f77736a738e9566bd1ebd1b46438ffb" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:25.195ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> but −2 does not have any real 6th roots.
</p><p>Every non-zero number <i>x</i>, real or <a href="/wiki/Complex_number" title="Complex number">complex</a>, has <i>n</i> different complex number <i>n</i>th roots.  (In the case <i>x</i> is real, this count includes any real <i>n</i>th roots.) The only complex root of 0 is 0.
</p><p>The <i>n</i>th roots of almost all numbers (all integers except the <i>n</i>th powers, and all rationals except the quotients of two <i>n</i>th powers) are <a href="/wiki/Irrational_number" title="Irrational number">irrational</a>.  For example,
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {2}}=1.414213562\ldots }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mn>2</mn>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1.414213562</mn>
<mo>…<!-- … --></mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt {2}}=1.414213562\ldots }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\sqrt {2}}=1.414213562\ldots " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d273e2a591fe737313334b80105a307e6db5553d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:21.579ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>All <i>n</i>th roots of integers are <a href="/wiki/Algebraic_number" title="Algebraic number">algebraic numbers</a>.
</p><p>The term <b>surd</b> traces back to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khw%C4%81rizm%C4%AB" title="Khwārizmī">al-Khwārizmī</a> (c. 825), who referred to rational and irrational numbers as <i>audible</i> and <i>inaudible</i>, respectively. This later led to the Arabic word "<span title="Tajik-language text"><span dir="rtl" lang="tg-Arab">أصم</span></span>" (<i>asamm</i>, meaning "deaf" or "dumb") for <i>irrational number</i> being translated into Latin as "surdus" (meaning "deaf" or "mute"). <a href="/wiki/Gerard_of_Cremona" title="Gerard of Cremona">Gerard of Cremona</a> (c. 1150), <a href="/wiki/Fibonacci" title="Fibonacci">Fibonacci</a> (1202), and then <a href="/wiki/Robert_Recorde" title="Robert Recorde">Robert Recorde</a> (1551) all used the term to refer to <i>unresolved irrational roots</i>, that is, expressions of the form <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{i}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mroot>
<mi>i</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</mroot>
</mrow>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{i}},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{i}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f639f1361b993b324d8e15ff02b9a7f392ad3cf2" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.385ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> in which <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle n}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>n</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle n}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="n" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.395ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle i}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>i</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle i}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="i" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/add78d8608ad86e54951b8c8bd6c8d8416533d20" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.802ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> are integer numerals and the whole expression denotes an irrational number.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quadratic_irrational_numbers" title="Quadratic irrational numbers">Quadratic irrational numbers</a>, that is, irrational numbers of the form <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {i}},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mi>i</mi>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt {i}},}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {i}},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1b56ef06140a7ebd4158c1b0782cd83f019bfbcf" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.385ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> are also known as "quadratic surds".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Square_roots">Square roots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Square roots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Square-root_function.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="440" decoding="async" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Square-root_function.svg/220px-Square-root_function.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Square-root_function.svg/330px-Square-root_function.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Square-root_function.svg/440px-Square-root_function.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Square-root_function.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The graph <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle y=\pm {\sqrt {x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>y</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mo>±<!-- ± --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mi>x</mi>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y=\pm {\sqrt {x}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="y=\pm {\sqrt {x}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1f65592780916b5eb3c41a21a66ee26ed7de05a2" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:9.328ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Square_root" title="Square root">Square root</a></div>
<p>A <b>square root</b> of a number <i>x</i> is a number <i>r</i> which, when <a href="/wiki/Square_(algebra)" title="Square (algebra)">squared</a>, becomes <i>x</i>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r^{2}=x.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>r</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r^{2}=x.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle r^{2}=x.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/97566cd6d91da0b946484c06ce8b2fe741664c02" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.178ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Every positive real number has two square roots, one positive and one negative.  For example, the two square roots of 25 are 5 and −5.  The positive square root is also known as the <b>principal square root</b>, and is denoted with a radical sign:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {25}}=5.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mn>25</mn>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>5.</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt {25}}=5.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {25}}=5.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/21ccdc1d8170229d7025384971da4ad211d7c25f" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:9.169ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Since the square of every real number is nonnegative, negative numbers do not have real square roots.  However, for every negative real number there are two <a href="/wiki/Imaginary_number" title="Imaginary number">imaginary</a> square roots.  For example, the square roots of −25 are 5<i>i</i> and −5<i>i</i>, where <i><a href="/wiki/Imaginary_unit" title="Imaginary unit">i</a></i> represents a number whose square is <span class="texhtml">−1</span>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cube_roots">Cube roots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Cube roots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cube-root_function.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="440" data-file-width="520" decoding="async" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Cube-root_function.svg/220px-Cube-root_function.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Cube-root_function.svg/330px-Cube-root_function.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Cube-root_function.svg/440px-Cube-root_function.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cube-root_function.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The graph <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle y={\sqrt[{3}]{x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cube_root" title="Cube root">Cube root</a></div>
<p>A <b>cube root</b> of a number <i>x</i> is a number <i>r</i> whose <a href="/wiki/Cube_(algebra)" title="Cube (algebra)">cube</a> is <i>x</i>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r^{3}=x.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>r</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>3</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r^{3}=x.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle r^{3}=x.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/db2ac05166dc4eef4955b7938f057bc5028ad543" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:7.178ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Every real number <i>x</i> has exactly one real cube root, written <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{3}]{x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>

</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{3}]{8}}=2}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>Every real number has two additional <a href="/wiki/Complex_number" title="Complex number">complex</a> cube roots.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Identities_and_properties">Identities and properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Identities and properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Expressing the degree of an <i>n</i>th root in its exponent form, as in <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x^{1/n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x^{1/n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x^{1/n}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0acb961738e6ffb034db9b37250579f700c49d8e" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:4.192ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, makes it easier to manipulate powers and roots. If <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{a^{m}}}=(a^{m})^{1/n}=a^{m/n}=(a^{1/n})^{m}=({\sqrt[{n}]{a}})^{m}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{a^{m}}}=(a^{m})^{1/n}=a^{m/n}=(a^{1/n})^{m}=({\sqrt[{n}]{a}})^{m}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/db6ea037832c3df199f25395b7043ea18927905b" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:44.398ex; height:3.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Every non-negative number has exactly one non-negative real <i>n</i>th root, and so the rules for operations with surds involving non-negative radicands <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>a</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="a" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ffd2487510aa438433a2579450ab2b3d557e5edc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.23ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>b</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f11423fbb2e967f986e36804a8ae4271734917c3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.998ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> are straightforward within the real numbers:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\sqrt[{n}]{ab}}&amp;={\sqrt[{n}]{a}}{\sqrt[{n}]{b}}\\{\sqrt[{n}]{\frac {a}{b}}}&amp;={\frac {\sqrt[{n}]{a}}{\sqrt[{n}]{b}}}\end{aligned}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\sqrt[{n}]{ab}}&amp;={\sqrt[{n}]{a}}{\sqrt[{n}]{b}}\\{\sqrt[{n}]{\frac {a}{b}}}&amp;={\frac {\sqrt[{n}]{a}}{\sqrt[{n}]{b}}}\end{aligned}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b1b645cc98d9626d9b49b01acfb20f4a5efb3abf" style="vertical-align: -4.505ex; width:14.339ex; height:10.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Subtleties can occur when taking the <i>n</i>th roots of negative or <a href="/wiki/Complex_number" title="Complex number">complex numbers</a>. For instance:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {-1}}\times {\sqrt {-1}}\neq {\sqrt {-1\times -1}}=1,\quad }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>Since the rule <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{a}}\times {\sqrt[{n}]{b}}={\sqrt[{n}]{ab}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Simplified_form_of_a_radical_expression">Simplified form of a radical expression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Simplified form of a radical expression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A non-nested radical expression is said to be in <b>simplified form</b> if<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li>There is no factor of the radicand that can be written as a power greater than or equal to the index.</li>
<li>There are no fractions under the radical sign.</li>
<li>There are no radicals in the denominator.</li></ol>
<p>For example, to write the radical expression <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {\tfrac {32}{5}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<msqrt>
<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
<mfrac>
<mn>32</mn>
<mn>5</mn>
</mfrac>
</mstyle>
</msqrt>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt {\tfrac {32}{5}}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\sqrt {\tfrac {32}{5}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4d501d37a975f551c14bab7228d2c8253a3a9c70" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:4.804ex; height:4.843ex;"/></span> in simplified form, we can proceed as follows. First, look for a perfect square under the square root sign and remove it:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {\tfrac {32}{5}}}={\sqrt {\tfrac {16\cdot 2}{5}}}={\sqrt {16}}\cdot {\sqrt {\tfrac {2}{5}}}=4{\sqrt {\tfrac {2}{5}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {\tfrac {32}{5}}}={\sqrt {\tfrac {16\cdot 2}{5}}}={\sqrt {16}}\cdot {\sqrt {\tfrac {2}{5}}}=4{\sqrt {\tfrac {2}{5}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bd12b848ee02f1601091b1cf314c51fc95b92b03" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:35.249ex; height:4.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>

</p>

<p>When there is a denominator involving surds it is always possible to find a factor to multiply both numerator and denominator by to simplify the expression.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> For instance using the <a href="/wiki/Factorization#Sum/difference_of_two_cubes" title="Factorization">factorization of the sum of two cubes</a>:

<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {1}{{\sqrt[{3}]{a}}+{\sqrt[{3}]{b}}}}={\frac {{\sqrt[{3}]{a^{2}}}-{\sqrt[{3}]{ab}}+{\sqrt[{3}]{b^{2}}}}{\left({\sqrt[{3}]{a}}+{\sqrt[{3}]{b}}\right)\left({\sqrt[{3}]{a^{2}}}-{\sqrt[{3}]{ab}}+{\sqrt[{3}]{b^{2}}}\right)}}={\frac {{\sqrt[{3}]{a^{2}}}-{\sqrt[{3}]{ab}}+{\sqrt[{3}]{b^{2}}}}{a+b}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>Let <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r=p/q}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

Then <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{r}}={\sqrt[{n}]{p}}/{\sqrt[{n}]{q}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infinite_series">Infinite series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Infinite series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The radical or root may be represented by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infinite_series" title="Infinite series">infinite series</a>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle (1+x)^{\frac {s}{t}}=\sum _{n=0}^{\infty }{\frac {\prod _{k=0}^{n-1}(s-kt)}{n!t^{n}}}x^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle (1+x)^{\frac {s}{t}}=\sum _{n=0}^{\infty }{\frac {\prod _{k=0}^{n-1}(s-kt)}{n!t^{n}}}x^{n}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ec5bb95748f261639ef5778c580e6f0af8d0880b" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:32.365ex; height:7.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>with <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle |x|&lt;1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Computing_principal_roots">Computing principal roots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Computing principal roots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Using_Newton.27s_method"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Using_Newton's_method">Using Newton's method</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Using Newton's method">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i></span>th root of a number <span class="texhtml"><i>A</i></span> can be computed with <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_method" title="Newton's method">Newton's method</a>, which starts with an initial guess <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>0</sub></span> and then iterates using the <a href="/wiki/Recurrence_relation" title="Recurrence relation">recurrence relation</a>
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x_{k+1}=x_{k}-{\frac {x_{k}^{n}-A}{nx_{k}^{n-1}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>k</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<msubsup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msubsup>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>A</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow>
<mi>n</mi>
<msubsup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msubsup>
</mrow>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x_{k+1}=x_{k}-{\frac {x_{k}^{n}-A}{nx_{k}^{n-1}}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle x_{k+1}=x_{k}-{\frac {x_{k}^{n}-A}{nx_{k}^{n-1}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d31f4bc6367f18903b64976c99afec01f1ea5363" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:20.844ex; height:7.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>until the desired precision is reached. For computational efficiency, the recurrence relation is commonly rewritten 
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x_{k+1}={\frac {n-1}{n}}\,x_{k}+{\frac {A}{n}}\,{\frac {1}{x_{k}^{n-1}}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msub>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>k</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
<mi>n</mi>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
<msub>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>+</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mi>A</mi>
<mi>n</mi>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mn>1</mn>
<msubsup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>k</mi>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</msubsup>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x_{k+1}={\frac {n-1}{n}}\,x_{k}+{\frac {A}{n}}\,{\frac {1}{x_{k}^{n-1}}}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle x_{k+1}={\frac {n-1}{n}}\,x_{k}+{\frac {A}{n}}\,{\frac {1}{x_{k}^{n-1}}}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6b4cc95fe4db62eb0624a6e622f720662f9606cd" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:28.595ex; height:6.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>This allows to have only one <a href="/wiki/Exponentiation" title="Exponentiation">exponentiation</a>, and to compute once for all the first factor of each term.
</p><p>For example, to find the fifth root of 34, we plug in <span class="texhtml"><i>n</i> = 5, <i>A</i> = 34</span> and <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>0</sub> = 2</span> (initial guess). The first 5 iterations are, approximately:
<br/>
<span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>0</sub> = 2</span>
<br/>
<span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>1</sub> = 2.025</span>
<br/>
<span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>2</sub> = 2.02439 7...</span>
<br/>
<span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>3</sub> = 2.02439 7458...</span>
<br/>
<span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>4</sub> = 2.02439 74584 99885 04251 08172...</span>
<br/>
<span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>5</sub> = 2.02439 74584 99885 04251 08172 45541 93741 91146 21701 07311 8...</span>
<br/>
(All correct digits shown.)
</p><p>The approximation <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>4</sub></span> is accurate to 25 decimal places and <span class="texhtml"><i>x</i><sub>5</sub></span> is good for 51. 
</p><p>Newton's method can be modified to produce various <a href="/wiki/Generalized_continued_fraction#Roots_of_positive_numbers" title="Generalized continued fraction">generalized continued fractions</a> for the <i>n</i>th root. For example,
</p>

<h3><span id="Digit-by-digit_calculation_of_principal_roots_of_decimal_.28base_10.29_numbers"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Digit-by-digit_calculation_of_principal_roots_of_decimal_(base_10)_numbers">Digit-by-digit calculation of principal roots of decimal (base 10) numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Digit-by-digit calculation of principal roots of decimal (base 10) numbers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PascalForDecimalRoots.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="120" data-file-width="240" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/PascalForDecimalRoots.svg/220px-PascalForDecimalRoots.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/PascalForDecimalRoots.svg/330px-PascalForDecimalRoots.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/PascalForDecimalRoots.svg/440px-PascalForDecimalRoots.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PascalForDecimalRoots.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pascal%27s_triangle" title="Pascal's triangle">Pascal's Triangle</a> showing <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle P(4,1)=4}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>P</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mn>4</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>

<mn>4</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P(4,1)=4}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="P(4,1)=4" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b841cdb2c861763e0e9f09d28d568adbecbbab0d" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.174ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>.</div></div></div>
<p>Building on the <a href="/wiki/Methods_of_computing_square_roots#Decimal_(base_10)" title="Methods of computing square roots">digit-by-digit calculation of a square root</a>, it can be seen that the formula used there, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x(20p+x)\leq c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

<mn>20</mn>
<mi>p</mi>
<mo>+</mo>

<mi>c</mi>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x(20p+x)\leq c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4cfe39e34c2c6ee28294d1ff2195e3dfbca33cac" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:14.909ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, or <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x^{2}+20xp\leq c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>

<mn>20</mn>
<mi>x</mi>
<mi>p</mi>
<mo>≤<!-- ≤ --></mo>
<mi>c</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x^{2}+20xp\leq c}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x^{2}+20xp\leq c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cd3b37b91f0f08498167cb382c372e2944e55892" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:14.154ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>, follows a pattern involving Pascal's triangle.  For the <i>n</i>th root of a number <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle P(n,i)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mi>n</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P(n,i)}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="P(n,i)" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d2315f4ec75ea3037b5cf5c71ab7c4f88004c12e" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:6.786ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> is defined as the value of element <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle i}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>i</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle i}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="i" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/add78d8608ad86e54951b8c8bd6c8d8416533d20" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.802ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> in row <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle n}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>n</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle n}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="n" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.395ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> of Pascal's Triangle such that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle P(4,1)=4}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>P</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mn>4</mn>
<mo>,</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>4</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle P(4,1)=4}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="P(4,1)=4" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b841cdb2c861763e0e9f09d28d568adbecbbab0d" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.174ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, we can rewrite the expression as <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \sum _{i=0}^{n-1}10^{i}P(n,i)p^{i}x^{n-i}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<munderover>
<mo>∑<!-- ∑ --></mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>0</mn>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mrow>
</munderover>
<msup>
<mn>10</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mi>P</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mi>i</mi>
<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
<msup>
<mi>p</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mi>i</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \sum _{i=0}^{n-1}10^{i}P(n,i)p^{i}x^{n-i}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\sum _{i=0}^{n-1}10^{i}P(n,i)p^{i}x^{n-i}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/000d6d39fce76fabc686702ebea16892d10b5028" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:20.016ex; height:7.343ex;"/></span>.  For convenience, call the result of this expression <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle y}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>y</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="y" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b8a6208ec717213d4317e666f1ae872e00620a0d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.155ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>.  Using this more general expression, any positive principal root can be computed, digit-by-digit, as follows.
</p><p>Write the original number in decimal form. The numbers are written similar to the <a href="/wiki/Long_division" title="Long division">long division</a> algorithm, and, as in long division, the root will be written on the line above. Now separate the digits into groups of digits equating to the root being taken, starting from the decimal point and going both left and right. The decimal point of the root will be above the decimal point of the radicand. One digit of the root will appear above each group of digits of the original number.
</p><p>Beginning with the left-most group of digits, do the following procedure for each group:
</p>
<ol><li>Starting on the left, bring down the most significant (leftmost) group of digits not yet used (if all the digits have been used, write "0" the number of times required to make a group) and write them to the right of the remainder from the previous step (on the first step, there will be no remainder). In other words, multiply the remainder by <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle 10^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mn>10</mn>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle 10^{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="10^{n}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/eeff06a7c9ad9455cb809047cfc97a92c51e1bf7" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:3.543ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> and add the digits from the next group. This will be the <b>current value <i>c</i></b>.</li>
<li>Find <i>p</i> and <i>x</i>, as follows:
<ul><li>Let <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>p</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle p}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="p" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81eac1e205430d1f40810df36a0edffdc367af36" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:1.259ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> be the <b>part of the root found so far</b>, ignoring any decimal point. (For the first step, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle p=0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>p</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>0</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle p=0}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="p=0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b3e6ac10fa45fb984d886065f959a6bdd467b5e8" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:5.52ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span>).</li>
<li>Determine the greatest digit <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> such that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle y\leq c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>y</mi>
<mo>≤<!-- ≤ --></mo>
<mi>c</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y\leq c}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="y\leq c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/602c121cbacae4c9b48807a3baf4dece313dca2b" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:5.261ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>.</li>
<li>Place the digit <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.33ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> as the next digit of the root, i.e., above the group of digits you just brought down. Thus the next <i>p</i> will be the old <i>p</i> times 10 plus <i>x</i>.</li></ul></li>
<li>Subtract <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle y}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>y</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle y}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="y" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b8a6208ec717213d4317e666f1ae872e00620a0d" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:1.155ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> from <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle c}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>c</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle c}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="c" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/86a67b81c2de995bd608d5b2df50cd8cd7d92455" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.007ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> to form a new remainder.</li>
<li>If the remainder is zero and there are no more digits to bring down, then the algorithm has terminated. Otherwise go back to step 1 for another iteration.</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Examples">Examples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Examples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
