<p><b>Find the square root of 152.2756.</b>
</p>
<pre>        <u>  1  2. 3  4 </u>
    <u> </u>  /
     \/  01 52.27 56
</pre>
<pre>         01                   10<sup>0</sup>·1·0<sup>0</sup>·1<sup>2</sup> + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·0<sup>1</sup>·1<sup>1</sup>     ≤      1   &lt;   10<sup>0</sup>·1·0<sup>0</sup>·2<sup>2</sup>   + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·0<sup>1</sup>·2<sup>1</sup>         x = 1
        <u> 01 </u>                     y = 10<sup>0</sup>·1·0<sup>0</sup>·1<sup>2</sup>   + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·0<sup>1</sup>·1<sup>1</sup>   =  1 +    0   =     1
         00 52                10<sup>0</sup>·1·1<sup>0</sup>·2<sup>2</sup> + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·1<sup>1</sup>·2<sup>1</sup>     ≤     52   &lt;   10<sup>0</sup>·1·1<sup>0</sup>·3<sup>2</sup>   + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·1<sup>1</sup>·3<sup>1</sup>         x = 2
        <u> 00 44 </u>                  y = 10<sup>0</sup>·1·1<sup>0</sup>·2<sup>2</sup>   + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·1<sup>1</sup>·2<sup>1</sup>   =  4 +   40   =    44
            08 27             10<sup>0</sup>·1·12<sup>0</sup>·3<sup>2</sup> + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·12<sup>1</sup>·3<sup>1</sup>   ≤    827   &lt;   10<sup>0</sup>·1·12<sup>0</sup>·4<sup>2</sup>  + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·12<sup>1</sup>·4<sup>1</sup>        x = 3
           <u> 07 29 </u>               y = 10<sup>0</sup>·1·12<sup>0</sup>·3<sup>2</sup>  + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·12<sup>1</sup>·3<sup>1</sup>  =  9 +  720   =   729
               98 56          10<sup>0</sup>·1·123<sup>0</sup>·4<sup>2</sup> + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·123<sup>1</sup>·4<sup>1</sup> ≤   9856   &lt;   10<sup>0</sup>·1·123<sup>0</sup>·5<sup>2</sup> + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·123<sup>1</sup>·5<sup>1</sup>       x = 4
              <u> 98 56 </u>            y = 10<sup>0</sup>·1·123<sup>0</sup>·4<sup>2</sup> + 10<sup>1</sup>·2·123<sup>1</sup>·4<sup>1</sup> = 16 + 9840   =  9856
               00 00          Algorithm terminates: Answer is 12.34
</pre>
<p><b>Find the cube root of 4192 to the nearest hundredth.</b>
</p>
<pre>     <u>   1   6.  1   2   4</u>
 <u>3</u>  /
  \/  004 192.000 000 000
</pre>
<pre>      004                      10<sup>0</sup>·1·0<sup>0</sup>·1<sup>3</sup>    +  10<sup>1</sup>·3·0<sup>1</sup>·1<sup>2</sup>   + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·0<sup>2</sup>·1<sup>1</sup>    ≤          4  &lt;  10<sup>0</sup>·1·0<sup>0</sup>·2<sup>3</sup>     + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·0<sup>1</sup>·2<sup>2</sup>    + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·0<sup>2</sup>·2<sup>1</sup>     x = 1
     <u> 001 </u>                        y = 10<sup>0</sup>·1·0<sup>0</sup>·1<sup>3</sup>   + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·0<sup>1</sup>·1<sup>2</sup>   + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·0<sup>2</sup>·1<sup>1</sup>   =   1 +      0 +          0   =          1
      003 192                  10<sup>0</sup>·1·1<sup>0</sup>·6<sup>3</sup>    +  10<sup>1</sup>·3·1<sup>1</sup>·6<sup>2</sup>   + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·1<sup>2</sup>·6<sup>1</sup>    ≤       3192  &lt;  10<sup>0</sup>·1·1<sup>0</sup>·7<sup>3</sup>     + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·1<sup>1</sup>·7<sup>2</sup>    + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·1<sup>2</sup>·7<sup>1</sup>     x = 6
     <u> 003 096 </u>                    y = 10<sup>0</sup>·1·1<sup>0</sup>·6<sup>3</sup>   + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·1<sup>1</sup>·6<sup>2</sup>   + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·1<sup>2</sup>·6<sup>1</sup>   = 216 +  1,080 +      1,800   =      3,096
          096 000              10<sup>0</sup>·1·16<sup>0</sup>·1<sup>3</sup>   + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·16<sup>1</sup>·1<sup>2</sup>   + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·16<sup>2</sup>·1<sup>1</sup>   ≤      96000  &lt;  10<sup>0</sup>·1·16<sup>0</sup>·2<sup>3</sup>   + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·16<sup>1</sup>·2<sup>2</sup>   + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·16<sup>2</sup>·2<sup>1</sup>    x = 1
         <u> 077 281 </u>                y = 10<sup>0</sup>·1·16<sup>0</sup>·1<sup>3</sup>  + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·16<sup>1</sup>·1<sup>2</sup>  + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·16<sup>2</sup>·1<sup>1</sup>  =   1 +    480 +     76,800   =     77,281
          018 719 000          10<sup>0</sup>·1·161<sup>0</sup>·2<sup>3</sup>  + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·161<sup>1</sup>·2<sup>2</sup>  + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·161<sup>2</sup>·2<sup>1</sup>  ≤   18719000  &lt;  10<sup>0</sup>·1·161<sup>0</sup>·3<sup>3</sup>  + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·161<sup>1</sup>·3<sup>2</sup>  + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·161<sup>2</sup>·3<sup>1</sup>   x = 2
             <u> 015 571 928 </u>        y = 10<sup>0</sup>·1·161<sup>0</sup>·2<sup>3</sup> + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·161<sup>1</sup>·2<sup>2</sup> + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·161<sup>2</sup>·2<sup>1</sup> =   8 + 19,320 + 15,552,600   = 15,571,928
              003 147 072 000  10<sup>0</sup>·1·1612<sup>0</sup>·4<sup>3</sup> + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·1612<sup>1</sup>·4<sup>2</sup> + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·1612<sup>2</sup>·4<sup>1</sup> ≤ 3147072000  &lt;  10<sup>0</sup>·1·1612<sup>0</sup>·5<sup>3</sup> + 10<sup>1</sup>·3·1612<sup>1</sup>·5<sup>2</sup> + 10<sup>2</sup>·3·1612<sup>2</sup>·5<sup>1</sup>  x = 4
                               The desired precision is achieved:
                               The cube root of 4192 is about 16.12
</pre>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logarithmic_calculation">Logarithmic calculation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Logarithmic calculation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The principal <i>n</i>th root of a positive number can be computed using <a href="/wiki/Logarithm" title="Logarithm">logarithms</a>. Starting from the equation that defines <i>r</i> as an <i>n</i>th root of <i>x</i>, namely <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r^{n}=x,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>r</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r^{n}=x,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="r^{n}=x," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c22cbcdc8f114887cf0ceeb723bb9624c6f132e2" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:7.342ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span> with <i>x</i> positive and therefore its principal root <i>r</i> also positive, one takes logarithms of both sides (any <a href="/wiki/Logarithm#Particular_bases" title="Logarithm">base of the logarithm</a> will do) to obtain
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle n\log _{b}r=\log _{b}x\quad \quad {\text{hence}}\quad \quad \log _{b}r={\frac {\log _{b}x}{n}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>n</mi>
<msub>
<mi>log</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>b</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>r</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<msub>
<mi>log</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>b</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mspace width="1em"></mspace>
<mspace width="1em"></mspace>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mtext>hence</mtext>
</mrow>
<mspace width="1em"></mspace>
<mspace width="1em"></mspace>
<msub>
<mi>log</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>b</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>r</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<msub>
<mi>log</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>b</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>x</mi>
</mrow>
<mi>n</mi>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle n\log _{b}r=\log _{b}x\quad \quad {\text{hence}}\quad \quad \log _{b}r={\frac {\log _{b}x}{n}}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle n\log _{b}r=\log _{b}x\quad \quad {\text{hence}}\quad \quad \log _{b}r={\frac {\log _{b}x}{n}}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4179e4d37709a4daead660119bcc56ba783fd630" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:46.764ex; height:5.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>The root <i>r</i> is recovered from this by taking the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antilog" title="Antilog">antilog</a>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r=b^{{\frac {1}{n}}\log _{b}x}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>r</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mn>1</mn>
<mi>n</mi>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<msub>
<mi>log</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>b</mi>
</mrow>
</msub>
<mo>⁡<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
<mi>x</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle r=b^{{\frac {1}{n}}\log _{b}x}.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle r=b^{{\frac {1}{n}}\log _{b}x}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/731ba9105c64bbe834160c9dd59a97441227e949" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:12.213ex; height:3.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>(Note: That formula shows <i>b</i> raised to the power of the result of the division, not <i>b</i> multiplied by the result of the division.)
</p><p>For the case in which <i>x</i> is negative and <i>n</i> is odd, there is one real root <i>r</i> which is also negative. This can be found by first multiplying both sides of the defining equation by −1 to obtain <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle |r|^{n}=|x|,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>r</mi>
<msup>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo stretchy="false">|</mo>
</mrow>
<mo>,</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle |r|^{n}=|x|,}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle |r|^{n}=|x|,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/070955f8d31c41a72920225b4da754731e240c4c" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:9.929ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> then proceeding as before to find |<i>r</i>|, and using <span class="nowrap"><i>r</i> = −|<i>r</i>|</span>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geometric_constructibility">Geometric constructibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geometric constructibility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_mathematicians" title="Ancient Greek mathematicians">ancient Greek mathematicians</a> knew how to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compass-and-straightedge_construction" title="Compass-and-straightedge construction">use compass and straightedge</a> to construct a length equal to the square root of a given length, when an auxiliary line of unit length is given. In 1837 <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Wantzel" title="Pierre Wantzel">Pierre Wantzel</a> proved that an <i>n</i>th root of a given length cannot be constructed if <i>n</i> is not a power of 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Complex_roots">Complex roots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Complex roots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Every <a href="/wiki/Complex_number" title="Complex number">complex number</a> other than 0 has <i>n</i> different <i>n</i>th roots.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Square_roots_2">Square roots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Square roots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Imaginary2Root.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="480" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Imaginary2Root.svg/220px-Imaginary2Root.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Imaginary2Root.svg/330px-Imaginary2Root.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Imaginary2Root.svg/440px-Imaginary2Root.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Imaginary2Root.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The square roots of <i><b>i</b></i></div></div></div>
<p>The two square roots of a complex number are always negatives of each other. For example, the square roots of <span class="texhtml">−4</span> are <span class="texhtml">2<i>i</i></span> and <span class="texhtml">−2<i>i</i></span>, and the square roots of <span class="texhtml"><i>i</i></span> are
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\tfrac {1}{\sqrt {2}}}(1+i)\quad {\text{and}}\quad -{\tfrac {1}{\sqrt {2}}}(1+i).}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<p>A <i>principal</i> root of a complex number may be chosen in various ways, for example
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt {re^{i\theta }}}={\sqrt {r}}\cdot e^{i\theta /2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<p>which introduces a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Branch_cut" title="Branch cut">branch cut</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Complex_plane" title="Complex plane">complex plane</a> along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Positive_real_axis" title="Positive real axis">positive real axis</a> with the condition <span class="texhtml">0 ≤ <i>θ</i> &lt; 2<span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">π</span></span>, or along the negative real axis with <span class="texhtml">−<span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">π</span> &lt; <i>θ</i> ≤ <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">π</span></span>.
</p><p>Using the first(last) branch cut the principal square root <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \scriptstyle {\sqrt {z}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</msqrt>

</mstyle>
</mstyle>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\scriptstyle {\sqrt {z}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4822ea5fba80988907cf54af2c4c5e51ceffadd0" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.138ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> maps <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \scriptstyle z}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="1">
<mi>z</mi>
</mstyle>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \scriptstyle z}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\scriptstyle z" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ea1aac04b6044a6bc2aa0ca36b4580a19019d46e" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:0.769ex; height:1.343ex;"/></span> to the half plane with non-negative imaginary(real) part. The last branch cut is presupposed in mathematical software like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matlab" title="Matlab">Matlab</a> or <a href="/wiki/Scilab" title="Scilab">Scilab</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roots_of_unity">Roots of unity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Roots of unity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:3rd_roots_of_unity.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="610" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/3rd_roots_of_unity.svg/220px-3rd_roots_of_unity.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/3rd_roots_of_unity.svg/330px-3rd_roots_of_unity.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/3rd_roots_of_unity.svg/440px-3rd_roots_of_unity.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:3rd_roots_of_unity.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The three 3rd roots of 1</div></div></div>

For example, the square roots of unity are 1 and −1, and the fourth roots of unity are 1, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle i}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="nth_roots"><i>n</i>th roots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: nth roots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="333" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg/250px-Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg/375px-Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg/500px-Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Visualisation_complex_number_roots.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geometric representation of the 2nd to 6th roots of a complex number <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span>, in polar form <span class="nowrap"><span class="texhtml"><i>re</i><sup><i>iφ</i></sup></span> </span> where <span class="nowrap"><span class="texhtml"><i>r</i> = |<i>z</i> |</span></span> and <span class="nowrap"><span class="texhtml"><i>φ</i> = arg <i>z</i></span></span>. If <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">z</span> is real, <span class="nowrap"><span class="texhtml"><i>φ</i> = 0</span> or <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">π</span></span>. Principal roots are shown in black.</div></div></div>
<p>Every complex number has <i>n</i> different <i>n</i>th roots in the complex plane.  These are
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \eta ,\;\eta \omega ,\;\eta \omega ^{2},\;\ldots ,\;\eta \omega ^{n-1},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>η<!-- η --></mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mspace width="thickmathspace"></mspace>
<mi>η<!-- η --></mi>
<mi>ω<!-- ω --></mi>
<mo>,</mo>
<mspace width="thickmathspace"></mspace>
<mi>η<!-- η --></mi>
<msup>
<mi>ω<!-- ω --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>2</mn>
</mrow>

<p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polar_form" title="Polar form">polar form</a>, a single <i>n</i>th root may be found by the formula

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{re^{i\theta }}}={\sqrt[{n}]{r}}\cdot e^{i\theta /n}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fb634da6a458c0fdff9deb78d393ff2791ab3b7c" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:18.898ex; height:3.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>Here <i>r</i> is the magnitude (the modulus, also called the <a href="/wiki/Absolute_value" title="Absolute value">absolute value</a>) of the number whose root is to be taken; if the number can be written as <i>a+bi</i> then <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle r={\sqrt {a^{2}+b^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

</mrow>

Also, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \theta }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>θ<!-- θ --></mi>

</mrow>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\theta " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6e5ab2664b422d53eb0c7df3b87e1360d75ad9af" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is the angle formed as one pivots on the origin counterclockwise from the positive horizontal axis to a ray going from the origin to the number; it has the properties that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \cos \theta =a/r,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mi>sin</mi>

</mstyle>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\sin \theta =b/r," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ee2942e6cbe7ef79f8cbc5851f1c8960528102dd" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.287ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \tan \theta =b/a.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mi>tan</mi>

<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>a</mi>
<mo>.</mo>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \tan \theta =b/a.}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\tan \theta =b/a." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/99629f56d9f2784dac6f3c31c4b782b772e906d3" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:11.972ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>
</p><p>Thus finding <i>n</i>th roots in the complex plane can be segmented into two steps. First, the magnitude of all the <i>n</i>th roots is the <i>n</i>th root of the magnitude of the original number. Second, the angle between the positive horizontal axis and a ray from the origin to one of the <i>n</i>th roots is <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \theta /n}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>θ<!-- θ --></mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mo>/</mo>
</mrow>
<mi>n</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \theta /n}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\theta /n" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/20905d7e366eec7ab5418bec2cfc043584f32369" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:3.648ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>, where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle \theta }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>θ<!-- θ --></mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle \theta }</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="\theta " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6e5ab2664b422d53eb0c7df3b87e1360d75ad9af" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is the angle defined in the same way for the number whose root is being taken. Furthermore, all <i>n</i> of the <i>n</i>th roots are at equally spaced angles from each other.
</p><p>If <i>n</i> is even, a complex number's <i>n</i>th roots, of which there are an even number, come in <a href="/wiki/Additive_inverse" title="Additive inverse">additive inverse</a> pairs, so that if a number <i>r</i><sub>1</sub> is one of the <i>n</i>th roots then <i>r</i><sub>2</sub> =  –<i>r</i><sub>1</sub> is another. This is because raising the latter's coefficient –1 to the <i>n</i>th power for even <i>n</i> yields 1: that is, (–<i>r</i><sub>1</sub>)<sup><i>n</i></sup> = (–1)<sup><i>n</i></sup> × <i>r</i><sub>1</sub><sup><i>n</i></sup> = <i>r</i><sub>1</sub><sup><i>n</i></sup>.
</p><p>As with square roots, the formula above does not define a <a href="/wiki/Continuous_function" title="Continuous function">continuous function</a> over the entire complex plane, but instead has a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Branch_cut" title="Branch cut">branch cut</a> at points where <i>θ</i> / <i>n</i> is discontinuous.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Solving_polynomials">Solving polynomials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Solving polynomials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Root-finding_algorithm" title="Root-finding algorithm">Root-finding algorithm</a></div>
<p>It was once <a href="/wiki/Conjecture" title="Conjecture">conjectured</a> that all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polynomial_equation" title="Polynomial equation">polynomial equations</a> could be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algebraic_solution" title="Algebraic solution">solved algebraically</a> (that is, that all roots of a <a href="/wiki/Polynomial" title="Polynomial">polynomial</a> could be expressed in terms of a finite number of radicals and <a href="/wiki/Elementary_arithmetic" title="Elementary arithmetic">elementary operations</a>). However, while this is true for third degree polynomials (<a href="/wiki/Cubic_function" title="Cubic function">cubics</a>) and fourth degree polynomials (<a href="/wiki/Quartic_function" title="Quartic function">quartics</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Abel%E2%80%93Ruffini_theorem" title="Abel–Ruffini theorem">Abel–Ruffini theorem</a> (1824) shows that this is not true in general when the degree is 5 or greater. For example, the solutions of the equation
</p>
<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x^{5}=x+1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mn>5</mn>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>+</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x^{5}=x+1}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle x^{5}=x+1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bbb2478d09e89d1fc0370c2d3fa8488c9a5e84d4" style="vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:10.815ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>
<p>cannot be expressed in terms of radicals. (<i>cf.</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quintic_equation" title="Quintic equation">quintic equation</a>)
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Proof_of_irrationality_for_non-perfect_nth_power_x">Proof of irrationality for non-perfect <i>n</i>th power <i>x</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nth_root&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Proof of irrationality for non-perfect nth power x">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Assume that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mroot>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</mroot>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\sqrt[{n}]{x}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7b3ba2638d05cd9ed8dafae7e34986399e48ea99" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:3.266ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> is rational. That is, it can be reduced to a fraction <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {a}{b}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<mi>b</mi>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {a}{b}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\frac {a}{b}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9fbb66e57f89debc3cde3213de12228971148a93" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:2.066ex; height:4.843ex;"/></span>, where <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">a</span> and <span class="texhtml mvar" style="font-style:italic;">b</span> are integers without a common factor.
</p><p>This means that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x={\frac {a^{n}}{b^{n}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<msup>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x={\frac {a^{n}}{b^{n}}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle x={\frac {a^{n}}{b^{n}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6a17612d66adec36e70a10cbe6afc1bea7669b42" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:7.713ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>Since <i>x</i> is an integer, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle a^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>

</msup>

</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a^{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>

<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b^{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b^{n}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b8f8f52cd26bb201e02c8d1b3619a3a682f44dbc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.216ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>must share a common factor if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b\neq 1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>b</mi>
<mo>≠<!-- ≠ --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b\neq 1}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b \neq 1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/32a55c3a4b8eca743088b70c7c4d63c773f43c2b" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:5.258ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>. This means that if <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle b\neq 1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>b</mi>
<mo>≠<!-- ≠ --></mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b\neq 1}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="b \neq 1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/32a55c3a4b8eca743088b70c7c4d63c773f43c2b" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:5.258ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {a^{n}}{b^{n}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<msup>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {a^{n}}{b^{n}}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\frac {a^{n}}{b^{n}}}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6fafb316a65779077635b65898ad30f07f45c363" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:3.284ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span> is not in simplest form. Thus <i>b</i> should equal 1.
</p><p>Since <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle 1^{n}=1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<mo>=</mo>
<mn>1</mn>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle 1^{n}=1}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle 1^{n}=1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/93f80fba3de21e4d0bae42b0e9bbc88f3abbdcdc" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.642ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {n}{1}}=n}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mn>1</mn>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>n</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {n}{1}}=n}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\frac {n}{1}}=n}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4b9c183ef2f1ffc5f7f09b3ec7c3d7ade7af9cb1" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:6.724ex; height:4.676ex;"/></span>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {a^{n}}{b^{n}}}=a^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<msup>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
<msup>
<mi>b</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mfrac>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {a^{n}}{b^{n}}}=a^{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\frac {a^{n}}{b^{n}}}=a^{n}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/05b2df4ed68facd9cc6e41861103dfdcf5dff2df" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:8.831ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span>.
</p><p>This means that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle x=a^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<mi>x</mi>
<mo>=</mo>
<msup>
<mi>a</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</msup>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x=a^{n}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle x=a^{n}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/407e45335787b25bf78954908ec685cfb6b23622" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:6.876ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span> and thus, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}=a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mroot>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</mroot>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mi>a</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}=a}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}=a}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/39c0048b93aee48d4f00d14b120a98c1fbbcc67d" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:7.594ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span>. This implies that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mroot>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</mroot>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\sqrt[{n}]{x}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7b3ba2638d05cd9ed8dafae7e34986399e48ea99" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:3.266ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> is an integer. Since <i>x</i> is not a perfect <i>n</i>th power, this is impossible. Thus <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

<mroot>
<mi>x</mi>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mi>n</mi>
</mrow>
</mroot>
</mrow>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\sqrt[{n}]{x}}}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="{\sqrt[{n}]{x}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7b3ba2638d05cd9ed8dafae7e34986399e48ea99" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:3.266ex; height:3.009ex;"/></span> is irrational.
</p>

</li>
</ol></div></div>
